I've uploaded a python code repository in the directory /testbed/repo. Consider the following PR description:

<pr_description>
`cp` is is not properly cleaning existing file
I use the following command to get a "buffer" for my current clipboard stuff, which i use elsewhere - `wl-paste --watch cp /dev/stdin tmp`

when i was using gnu cp, with each clipboard copy, the `tmp` file is rewritten appropriately (old stuff cleaned, new stuff written). with uutils cp, old stuff partially remains. if original stuff was `n` characters long, and new content is `n'` (`n' < n`), then only first `n'` characters are rewritten, `n - n'` old characters remain. This seems very much dependent on how wl-paste is generateing output, but GNU cp, and busybox cp seem to handle it.

I know of `--remove-destination` option, and it works, but the way i am actually finally storing the buffer entries, is checking if the buffer file is modified, if modified, it handles the buffer. If i remove the file, the checker is thrown off.

My uutils package version is `0.0.29` from arch package, also tested `0.0.30`, same behaviour.

here is a video demo showing how existence of previous stuff in file 

![Image](https://github.com/user-attachments/assets/262b8f93-3c0e-4f2f-b7af-72cd3d3ea7e2)

</pr_description>

   121	            "{}",

   123	                "cp-error-backup-format",
   124	                HashMap::from([
   125	                    ("error".to_string(), self.0.clone()),
   126	                    ("exec".to_string(), uucore::execution_phrase().to_string())
   127	                ])
   128	            )
   129	        )
   130	    }
   131	}
   132	
   133	impl std::error::Error for BackupError {}
   134	
   135	impl UError for CpError {
   136	    fn code(&self) -> i32 {
   137	        EXIT_ERR
   138	    }
   139	}
   140	
   141	pub type CopyResult<T> = Result<T, CpError>;

   148	    #[default]

   152	/// Specifies whether files should be overwritten.
   153	#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, Eq, PartialEq)]
   154	pub enum OverwriteMode {
   155	    /// [Default] Always overwrite existing files
   156	    Clobber(ClobberMode),
   157	    /// Prompt before overwriting a file
   158	    Interactive(ClobberMode),
   159	    /// Never overwrite a file
   160	    NoClobber,
   161	}

   163	impl Default for OverwriteMode {
   164	    fn default() -> Self {
   165	        Self::Clobber(ClobberMode::default())
   166	    }
   167	}

   173	    Auto,

   175	}

   184	        #[cfg(not(any(target_os = "linux", target_os = "android", target_os = "macos")))]

   187	        }

   218	/// Preservation settings for various attributes
   219	///
   220	/// It should be derived from options as follows:
   221	///
   222	///  - if there is a list of attributes to preserve (i.e. `--preserve=ATTR_LIST`) parse that list with [`Attributes::parse_iter`],
   223	///  - if `-p` or `--preserve` is given without arguments, use [`Attributes::DEFAULT`],
   224	///  - if `-a`/`--archive` is passed, use [`Attributes::ALL`],
   225	///  - if `-d` is passed use [`Attributes::LINKS`],
   226	///  - otherwise, use [`Attributes::NONE`].
   227	///
   228	/// For full compatibility with GNU, these options should also combine. We
   229	/// currently only do a best effort imitation of that behavior, because it is
   230	/// difficult to achieve in clap, especially with `--no-preserve`.
   231	#[derive(Debug, PartialEq, Eq, Clone, Copy)]
   232	pub struct Attributes {
   233	    #[cfg(unix)]
   234	    pub ownership: Preserve,
   235	    pub mode: Preserve,
   236	    pub timestamps: Preserve,
   237	    pub context: Preserve,
   238	    pub links: Preserve,
   239	    pub xattr: Preserve,
   240	}
   241	
   242	impl Default for Attributes {
   243	    fn default() -> Self {
   244	        Self::NONE
   245	    }
   246	}
   247	
   248	#[derive(Clone, Copy, Debug, PartialEq, Eq)]
   249	pub enum Preserve {
   250	    // explicit means whether the --no-preserve flag is used or not to distinguish out the default value.
   251	    // e.g. --no-preserve=mode means mode = No { explicit = true }
   252	    No { explicit: bool },
   253	    Yes { required: bool },
   254	}
   255	
   256	impl PartialOrd for Preserve {
   257	    fn partial_cmp(&self, other: &Self) -> Option<Ordering> {
   258	        Some(self.cmp(other))
   259	    }
   260	}
   261	
   262	impl Ord for Preserve {
   263	    fn cmp(&self, other: &Self) -> Ordering {
   264	        match (self, other) {
   265	            (Self::No { .. }, Self::No { .. }) => Ordering::Equal,
   266	            (Self::Yes { .. }, Self::No { .. }) => Ordering::Greater,
   267	            (Self::No { .. }, Self::Yes { .. }) => Ordering::Less,
   268	            (
   269	                Self::Yes { required: req_self },
   270	                Self::Yes {
   271	                    required: req_other,
   272	                },
   273	            ) => req_self.cmp(req_other),
   274	        }
   275	    }
   276	}
   277	
   278	/// Options for the `cp` command
   279	///
   280	/// All options are public so that the options can be programmatically
   281	/// constructed by other crates, such as nushell. That means that this struct
   282	/// is part of our public API. It should therefore not be changed without good
   283	/// reason.
   284	///
   285	/// The fields are documented with the arguments that determine their value.
   286	#[allow(dead_code)]
   287	#[derive(Debug, Clone, Eq, PartialEq)]
   288	pub struct Options {
   289	    /// `--attributes-only`
   290	    pub attributes_only: bool,
   291	    /// `--backup[=CONTROL]`, `-b`
   292	    pub backup: BackupMode,
   293	    /// `--copy-contents`
   294	    pub copy_contents: bool,
   295	    /// `-H`
   296	    pub cli_dereference: bool,
   297	    /// Determines the type of copying that should be done
   298	    ///
   299	    /// Set by the following arguments:
   300	    ///  - `-l`, `--link`: [`CopyMode::Link`]
   301	    ///  - `-s`, `--symbolic-link`: [`CopyMode::SymLink`]
   302	    ///  - `-u`, `--update[=WHEN]`: [`CopyMode::Update`]
   303	    ///  - `--attributes-only`: [`CopyMode::AttrOnly`]
   304	    ///  - otherwise: [`CopyMode::Copy`]
   305	    pub copy_mode: CopyMode,
   306	    /// `-L`, `--dereference`
   307	    pub dereference: bool,
   308	    /// `-T`, `--no-target-dir`
   309	    pub no_target_dir: bool,
   310	    /// `-x`, `--one-file-system`
   311	    pub one_file_system: bool,
   312	    /// Specifies what to do with an existing destination
   313	    ///
   314	    /// Set by the following arguments:
   315	    ///  - `-i`, `--interactive`: [`OverwriteMode::Interactive`]
   316	    ///  - `-n`, `--no-clobber`: [`OverwriteMode::NoClobber`]
   317	    ///  - otherwise: [`OverwriteMode::Clobber`]
   318	    ///
   319	    /// The `Interactive` and `Clobber` variants have a [`ClobberMode`] argument,
   320	    /// set by the following arguments:
   321	    ///  - `-f`, `--force`: [`ClobberMode::Force`]
   322	    ///  - `--remove-destination`: [`ClobberMode::RemoveDestination`]
   323	    ///  - otherwise: [`ClobberMode::Standard`]
   324	    pub overwrite: OverwriteMode,
   325	    /// `--parents`
   326	    pub parents: bool,
   327	    /// `--sparse[=WHEN]`
   328	    pub sparse_mode: SparseMode,
   329	    /// `--strip-trailing-slashes`
   330	    pub strip_trailing_slashes: bool,
   331	    /// `--reflink[=WHEN]`
   332	    pub reflink_mode: ReflinkMode,
   333	    /// `--preserve=[=ATTRIBUTE_LIST]` and `--no-preserve=ATTRIBUTE_LIST`
   334	    pub attributes: Attributes,
   335	    /// `-R`, `-r`, `--recursive`
   336	    pub recursive: bool,
   337	    /// `-S`, `--suffix`
   338	    pub backup_suffix: String,
   339	    /// `-t`, `--target-directory`
   340	    pub target_dir: Option<PathBuf>,
   341	    /// `--update[=UPDATE]`
   342	    pub update: UpdateMode,
   343	    /// `--debug`
   344	    pub debug: bool,
   345	    /// `-v`, `--verbose`
   346	    pub verbose: bool,
   347	    /// `-g`, `--progress`
   348	    pub progress_bar: bool,
   349	    /// -Z
   350	    pub set_selinux_context: bool,
   351	    // --context
   352	    pub context: Option<String>,
   353	}
   354	
   355	impl Default for Options {
   356	    fn default() -> Self {
   357	        Self {
   358	            attributes_only: false,
   359	            backup: BackupMode::default(),
   360	            copy_contents: false,
   361	            cli_dereference: false,
   362	            copy_mode: CopyMode::default(),
   363	            dereference: false,
   364	            no_target_dir: false,
   365	            one_file_system: false,
   366	            overwrite: OverwriteMode::default(),
   367	            parents: false,
   368	            sparse_mode: SparseMode::default(),
   369	            strip_trailing_slashes: false,
   370	            reflink_mode: ReflinkMode::default(),
   371	            attributes: Attributes::default(),
   372	            recursive: false,
   373	            backup_suffix: backup_control::DEFAULT_BACKUP_SUFFIX.to_owned(),
   374	            target_dir: None,
   375	            update: UpdateMode::default(),
   376	            debug: false,
   377	            verbose: false,
   378	            progress_bar: false,
   379	            set_selinux_context: false,
   380	            context: None,
   381	        }
   382	    }
   383	}

   406	enum SparseDebug {

   408	    No,
   409	    Zeros,
   410	    SeekHole,
   411	    SeekHoleZeros,
   412	    Unsupported,

   415	/// Struct that contains the debug state for each action in a file copy operation.
   416	#[derive(Debug)]
   417	struct CopyDebug {
   418	    offload: OffloadReflinkDebug,
   419	    reflink: OffloadReflinkDebug,
   420	    sparse_detection: SparseDebug,
   421	}
   422	
   423	impl Display for OffloadReflinkDebug {
   424	    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> fmt::Result {
   425	        let msg = match self {
   426	            Self::No => get_message("cp-debug-enum-no"),
   427	            Self::Yes => get_message("cp-debug-enum-yes"),
   428	            Self::Avoided => get_message("cp-debug-enum-avoided"),
   429	            Self::Unsupported => get_message("cp-debug-enum-unsupported"),
   430	            Self::Unknown => get_message("cp-debug-enum-unknown"),
   431	        };
   432	        write!(f, "{}", msg)
   433	    }
   434	}
   435	
   436	impl Display for SparseDebug {
   437	    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> fmt::Result {
   438	        let msg = match self {
   439	            Self::No => get_message("cp-debug-enum-no"),
   440	            Self::Zeros => get_message("cp-debug-enum-zeros"),
   441	            Self::SeekHole => get_message("cp-debug-enum-seek-hole"),
   442	            Self::SeekHoleZeros => get_message("cp-debug-enum-seek-hole-zeros"),
   443	            Self::Unsupported => get_message("cp-debug-enum-unsupported"),
   444	            Self::Unknown => get_message("cp-debug-enum-unknown"),
   445	        };
   446	        write!(f, "{}", msg)
   447	    }
   448	}

   450	/// This function prints the debug information of a file copy operation if
   451	/// no hard link or symbolic link is required, and data copy is required.
   452	/// It prints the debug information of the offload, reflink, and sparse detection actions.
   453	fn show_debug(copy_debug: &CopyDebug) {
   454	    println!(
   455	        "{}",
   456	        get_message_with_args(
   457	            "cp-debug-copy-offload",
   458	            HashMap::from([
   459	                ("offload".to_string(), copy_debug.offload.to_string()),
   460	                ("reflink".to_string(), copy_debug.reflink.to_string()),
   461	                (
   462	                    "sparse".to_string(),
   463	                    copy_debug.sparse_detection.to_string()
   464	                ),
   465	            ])
   466	        )
   467	    );
   468	}

  2322	/// Calculates the permissions for the destination file in a copy operation.
  2323	///
  2324	/// If the destination file already exists, its current permissions are returned.
  2325	/// If the destination file does not exist, the source file's permissions are used,
  2326	/// with the `no-preserve` option and the umask taken into account on Unix platforms.
  2327	/// # Returns
  2328	///
  2329	/// * `Ok(Permissions)` - The calculated permissions for the destination file.
  2330	/// * `Err(CopyError)` - An error occurred while getting the metadata of the destination file.
  2331	///
  2332	// Allow unused variables for Windows (on options)
  2333	#[allow(unused_variables)]
  2334	fn calculate_dest_permissions(
  2335	    dest: &Path,
  2336	    source_metadata: &Metadata,
  2337	    options: &Options,
  2338	    context: &str,
  2339	) -> CopyResult<Permissions> {

  2343	            .map_err(|e| CpError::IoErrContext(e, context.to_owned()))?
  2344	            .permissions())

  2346	        #[cfg(unix)]
  2347	        {
  2348	            let mut permissions = source_metadata.permissions();
  2349	            let mode = handle_no_preserve_mode(options, permissions.mode());

  2166	    source: &Path,
  2167	    dest: &Path,
  2168	    options: &Options,
  2169	    context: &str,
  2170	    source_metadata: &Metadata,
  2171	    symlinked_files: &mut HashSet<FileInformation>,
  2172	    source_in_command_line: bool,
  2173	    source_is_fifo: bool,
  2174	    #[cfg(unix)] source_is_stream: bool,
  2175	) -> CopyResult<PerformedAction> {
  2176	    let source_is_symlink = source_metadata.is_symlink();
  2177	
  2178	    match options.copy_mode {
  2179	        CopyMode::Link => {
  2180	            if dest.exists() {
  2181	                let backup_path =
  2182	                    backup_control::get_backup_path(options.backup, dest, &options.backup_suffix);
  2183	                if let Some(backup_path) = backup_path {

  2185	                    fs::remove_file(dest)?;

  2187	                if options.overwrite == OverwriteMode::Clobber(ClobberMode::Force) {
  2188	                    fs::remove_file(dest)?;
  2189	                }
  2190	            }

  2192	                let resolved =
  2193	                    canonicalize(source, MissingHandling::Missing, ResolveMode::Physical).unwrap();

  2195	            } else {
  2196	                fs::hard_link(source, dest)
  2197	            }
  2198	            .map_err(|e| {
  2199	                CpError::IoErrContext(
  2200	                    e,
  2201	                    get_message_with_args(
  2202	                        "cp-error-cannot-create-hard-link",

  2215	                                    .quote()

  2219	                    ),

  2225	                source,
  2226	                dest,

  2228	                context,
  2229	                source_is_symlink,

  2231	                symlinked_files,

  2235	        }

  2672	    source: &Path,
  2673	    dest: &Path,
  2674	    options: &Options,
  2675	    context: &str,
  2676	    source_is_symlink: bool,
  2677	    source_is_fifo: bool,
  2678	    symlinked_files: &mut HashSet<FileInformation>,
  2679	    #[cfg(unix)] source_is_stream: bool,
  2680	) -> CopyResult<()> {
  2681	    if options.parents {
  2682	        let parent = dest.parent().unwrap_or(dest);
  2683	        fs::create_dir_all(parent)?;
  2684	    }
  2685	
  2686	    if path_ends_with_terminator(dest) && !dest.is_dir() {
  2687	        return Err(CpError::NotADirectory(dest.to_path_buf()));
  2688	    }
  2689	
  2690	    if source_is_fifo && options.recursive && !options.copy_contents {
  2691	        #[cfg(unix)]
  2692	        copy_fifo(dest, options.overwrite, options.debug)?;
  2693	    } else if source_is_symlink {
  2694	        copy_link(source, dest, symlinked_files)?;
  2695	    } else {

  2698	            dest,
  2699	            options.reflink_mode,
  2700	            options.sparse_mode,
  2701	            context,

  2703	            source_is_fifo,

  2705	            source_is_stream,
  2706	        )?;
  2707

  2709	            show_debug(&copy_debug);
  2710	        }
  2711	    }
  2712	
  2713	    Ok(())
  2714	}

  2716	// "Copies" a FIFO by creating a new one. This workaround is because Rust's
  2717	// built-in fs::copy does not handle FIFOs (see rust-lang/rust/issues/79390).
  2718	#[cfg(unix)]
  2719	fn copy_fifo(dest: &Path, overwrite: OverwriteMode, debug: bool) -> CopyResult<()> {
  2720	    if dest.exists() {
  2721	        overwrite.verify(dest, debug)?;
  2722	        fs::remove_file(dest)?;
  2723	    }
  2724	
  2725	    make_fifo(dest).map_err(|_| {
  2726	        get_message_with_args(
  2727	            "cp-error-cannot-create-fifo",
  2728	            HashMap::from([("path".to_string(), dest.quote().to_string())]),
  2729	        )
  2730	        .into()
  2731	    })
  2732	}
  2733	
  2734	fn copy_link(
  2735	    source: &Path,
  2736	    dest: &Path,
  2737	    symlinked_files: &mut HashSet<FileInformation>,
  2738	) -> CopyResult<()> {
  2739	    // Here, we will copy the symlink itself (actually, just recreate it)
  2740	    let link = fs::read_link(source)?;
  2741	    // we always need to remove the file to be able to create a symlink,
  2742	    // even if it is writeable.
  2743	    if dest.is_symlink() || dest.is_file() {
  2744	        fs::remove_file(dest)?;
  2745	    }
  2746	    symlink_file(&link, dest, symlinked_files)
  2747	}

  2749	/// Generate an error message if `target` is not the correct `target_type`
  2750	pub fn verify_target_type(target: &Path, target_type: &TargetType) -> CopyResult<()> {
  2751	    match (target_type, target.is_dir()) {
  2752	        (&TargetType::Directory, false) => Err(get_message_with_args(
  2753	            "cp-error-target-not-directory",
  2754	            HashMap::from([("target".to_string(), target.quote().to_string())]),
  2755	        )
  2756	        .into()),
  2757	        (&TargetType::File, true) => Err(get_message_with_args(
  2758	            "cp-error-cannot-overwrite-directory-with-non-directory",
  2759	            HashMap::from([("dir".to_string(), target.quote().to_string())]),
  2760	        )
  2761	        .into()),
  2762	        _ => Ok(()),
  2763	    }
  2764	}
  2765	
  2766	/// Remove the `root` prefix from `source` and prefix it with `target`
  2767	/// to create a file that is local to `target`
  2768	/// # Examples
  2769	///
  2770	/// ```ignore
  2771	/// assert!(uu_cp::localize_to_target(
  2772	///     &Path::new("a/source/"),
  2773	///     &Path::new("a/source/c.txt"),
  2774	///     &Path::new("target/"),
  2775	/// ).unwrap() == Path::new("target/c.txt"))
  2776	/// ```
  2777	pub fn localize_to_target(root: &Path, source: &Path, target: &Path) -> CopyResult<PathBuf> {
  2778	    let local_to_root = source.strip_prefix(root)?;
  2779	    Ok(target.join(local_to_root))
  2780	}
  2781	
  2782	/// Get the total size of a slice of files and directories.
  2783	///
  2784	/// This function is much like the `du` utility, by recursively getting the sizes of files in directories.
  2785	/// Files are not deduplicated when appearing in multiple sources. If `recursive` is set to `false`, the
  2786	/// directories in `paths` will be ignored.
  2787	fn disk_usage(paths: &[PathBuf], recursive: bool) -> io::Result<u64> {
  2788	    let mut total = 0;
  2789	    for p in paths {
  2790	        let md = fs::metadata(p)?;
  2791	        if md.file_type().is_dir() {
  2792	            if recursive {
  2793	                total += disk_usage_directory(p)?;
  2794	            }
  2795	        } else {
  2796	            total += md.len();
  2797	        }
  2798	    }
  2799	    Ok(total)
  2800	}
  2801	
  2802	/// A helper for `disk_usage` specialized for directories.
  2803	fn disk_usage_directory(p: &Path) -> io::Result<u64> {
  2804	    let mut total = 0;
  2805	
  2806	    for entry in fs::read_dir(p)? {
  2807	        let entry = entry?;
  2808	        if entry.file_type()?.is_dir() {
  2809	            total += disk_usage_directory(&entry.path())?;
  2810	        } else {
  2811	            total += entry.metadata()?.len();
  2812	        }
  2813	    }
  2814	
  2815	    Ok(total)
  2816	}

    23	/// The fallback behavior for [`clone`] on failed system call.
    24	#[derive(Clone, Copy)]
    25	enum CloneFallback {
    26	    /// Raise an error.
    27	    Error,
    28	
    29	    /// Use [`std::fs::copy`].
    30	    FSCopy,
    31	
    32	    /// Use sparse_copy
    33	    SparseCopy,
    34	
    35	    /// Use sparse_copy_without_hole
    36	    SparseCopyWithoutHole,
    37	}

    39	/// Type of method used for copying files
    40	#[derive(Clone, Copy)]
    41	enum CopyMethod {
    42	    /// Do a sparse copy
    43	    SparseCopy,
    44	    /// Use [`std::fs::copy`].
    45	    FSCopy,
    46	    /// Default (can either be sparse_copy or FSCopy)

    52	/// Use the Linux `ioctl_ficlone` API to do a copy-on-write clone.
    53	///
    54	/// `fallback` controls what to do if the system call fails.
    55	#[cfg(any(target_os = "linux", target_os = "android"))]
    56	fn clone<P>(source: P, dest: P, fallback: CloneFallback) -> std::io::Result<()>
    57	where
    58	    P: AsRef<Path>,
    59	{
    60	    let src_file = File::open(&source)?;
    61	    let dst_file = File::create(&dest)?;
    62	    let src_fd = src_file.as_raw_fd();
    63	    let dst_fd = dst_file.as_raw_fd();
    64	    // Using .try_into().unwrap() is required as glibc, musl & android all have different type for ioctl()
    65	    #[allow(clippy::unnecessary_fallible_conversions)]
    66	    let result = unsafe {
    67	        libc::ioctl(
    68	            dst_fd,
    69	            linux_raw_sys::ioctl::FICLONE.try_into().unwrap(),
    70	            src_fd,
    71	        )
    72	    };
    73	    if result == 0 {
    74	        return Ok(());
    75	    }
    76	    match fallback {
    77	        CloneFallback::Error => Err(std::io::Error::last_os_error()),
    78	        CloneFallback::FSCopy => std::fs::copy(source, dest).map(|_| ()),
    79	        CloneFallback::SparseCopy => sparse_copy(source, dest),
    80	        CloneFallback::SparseCopyWithoutHole => sparse_copy_without_hole(source, dest),
    81	    }
    82	}
    83	
    84	/// Checks whether a file contains any non null bytes i.e. any byte != 0x0
    85	/// This function returns a tuple of (bool, u64, u64) signifying a tuple of (whether a file has
    86	/// data, its size, no of blocks it has allocated in disk)
    87	#[cfg(any(target_os = "linux", target_os = "android"))]
    88	fn check_for_data(source: &Path) -> Result<(bool, u64, u64), std::io::Error> {
    89	    let mut src_file = File::open(source)?;
    90	    let metadata = src_file.metadata()?;
    91	
    92	    let size = metadata.size();
    93	    let blocks = metadata.blocks();
    94	    // checks edge case of virtual files in /proc which have a size of zero but contains data
    95	    if size == 0 {
    96	        let mut buf: Vec<u8> = vec![0; metadata.blksize() as usize]; // Directly use metadata.blksize()
    97	        let _ = src_file.read(&mut buf)?;
    98	        return Ok((buf.iter().any(|&x| x != 0x0), size, 0));
    99	    }
   100	
   101	    let src_fd = src_file.as_raw_fd();
   102	
   103	    let result = unsafe { libc::lseek(src_fd, 0, SEEK_DATA) };
   104	
   105	    match result {
   106	        -1 => Ok((false, size, blocks)), // No data found or end of file
   107	        _ if result >= 0 => Ok((true, size, blocks)), // Data found
   108	        _ => Err(std::io::Error::last_os_error()),
   109	    }
   110	}
   111	
   112	#[cfg(any(target_os = "linux", target_os = "android"))]
   113	/// Checks whether a file is sparse i.e. it contains holes, uses the crude heuristic blocks < size / 512
   114	/// Reference:`<https://doc.rust-lang.org/std/os/unix/fs/trait.MetadataExt.html#tymethod.blocks>`
   115	fn check_sparse_detection(source: &Path) -> Result<bool, std::io::Error> {
   116	    let src_file = File::open(source)?;
   117	    let metadata = src_file.metadata()?;
   118	    let size = metadata.size();
   119	    let blocks = metadata.blocks();
   120	
   121	    if blocks < size / 512 {
   122	        return Ok(true);
   123	    }
   124	    Ok(false)
   125	}
   126	
   127	/// Optimized sparse_copy, doesn't create holes for large sequences of zeros in non sparse_files
   128	/// Used when --sparse=auto
   129	#[cfg(any(target_os = "linux", target_os = "android"))]
   130	fn sparse_copy_without_hole<P>(source: P, dest: P) -> std::io::Result<()>
   131	where
   132	    P: AsRef<Path>,
   133	{
   134	    let src_file = File::open(source)?;
   135	    let dst_file = File::create(dest)?;
   136	    let dst_fd = dst_file.as_raw_fd();
   137	
   138	    let size = src_file.metadata()?.size();
   139	    if unsafe { libc::ftruncate(dst_fd, size.try_into().unwrap()) } < 0 {
   140	        return Err(std::io::Error::last_os_error());
   141	    }
   142	    let src_fd = src_file.as_raw_fd();
   143	    let mut current_offset: isize = 0;
   144	    // Maximize the data read at once to 16 MiB to avoid memory hogging with large files
   145	    // 16 MiB chunks should saturate an SSD
   146	    let step = std::cmp::min(size, 16 * 1024 * 1024) as usize;
   147	    let mut buf: Vec<u8> = vec![0x0; step];
   148	    loop {
   149	        let result = unsafe { libc::lseek(src_fd, current_offset.try_into().unwrap(), SEEK_DATA) }
   150	            .try_into()
   151	            .unwrap();
   152	
   153	        current_offset = result;
   154	        let hole: isize =
   155	            unsafe { libc::lseek(src_fd, current_offset.try_into().unwrap(), SEEK_HOLE) }
   156	                .try_into()
   157	                .unwrap();
   158	        if result == -1 || hole == -1 {
   159	            break;
   160	        }
   161	        if result <= -2 || hole <= -2 {
   162	            return Err(std::io::Error::last_os_error());
   163	        }
   164	        let len: isize = hole - current_offset;
   165	        // Read and write data in chunks of `step` while reusing the same buffer
   166	        for i in (0..len).step_by(step) {
   167	            // Ensure we don't read past the end of the file or the start of the next hole
   168	            let read_len = std::cmp::min((len - i) as usize, step);
   169	            let buf = &mut buf[..read_len];
   170	            src_file.read_exact_at(buf, (current_offset + i) as u64)?;
   171	            dst_file.write_all_at(buf, (current_offset + i) as u64)?;
   172	        }
   173	        current_offset = hole;
   174	    }
   175	    Ok(())
   176	}
   177	/// Perform a sparse copy from one file to another.
   178	/// Creates a holes for large sequences of zeros in non_sparse_files, used for --sparse=always
   179	#[cfg(any(target_os = "linux", target_os = "android"))]
   180	fn sparse_copy<P>(source: P, dest: P) -> std::io::Result<()>
   181	where
   182	    P: AsRef<Path>,
   183	{
   184	    let mut src_file = File::open(source)?;
   185	    let dst_file = File::create(dest)?;
   186	    let dst_fd = dst_file.as_raw_fd();
   187	
   188	    let size: usize = src_file.metadata()?.size().try_into().unwrap();
   189	    if unsafe { libc::ftruncate(dst_fd, size.try_into().unwrap()) } < 0 {
   190	        return Err(std::io::Error::last_os_error());
   191	    }
   192	
   193	    let blksize = dst_file.metadata()?.blksize();
   194	    let mut buf: Vec<u8> = vec![0; blksize.try_into().unwrap()];
   195	    let mut current_offset: usize = 0;
   196	
   197	    // TODO Perhaps we can employ the "fiemap ioctl" API to get the
   198	    // file extent mappings:
   199	    // https://www.kernel.org/doc/html/latest/filesystems/fiemap.html
   200	    while current_offset < size {
   201	        let this_read = src_file.read(&mut buf)?;
   202	        let buf = &buf[..this_read];
   203	        if buf.iter().any(|&x| x != 0) {
   204	            dst_file.write_all_at(buf, current_offset.try_into().unwrap())?;
   205	        }
   206	        current_offset += this_read;
   207	    }
   208	    Ok(())
   209	}

   211	#[cfg(any(target_os = "linux", target_os = "android"))]
   212	/// Checks whether an existing destination is a fifo
   213	fn check_dest_is_fifo(dest: &Path) -> bool {
   214	    // If our destination file exists and its a fifo , we do a standard copy .
   215	    let file_type = std::fs::metadata(dest);
   216	    match file_type {
   217	        Ok(f) => f.file_type().is_fifo(),
   218	
   219	        _ => false,
   220	    }
   221	}
   222	
   223	/// Copy the contents of a stream from `source` to `dest`. The `if_fifo` argument is used to
   224	/// determine if we need to modify the file's attributes before and after copying.
   225	fn copy_stream<P>(source: P, dest: P, is_fifo: bool) -> std::io::Result<u64>
   226	where
   227	    P: AsRef<Path>,
   228	{
   229	    // For some reason,
   230	    //
   231	    //     cp --preserve=ownership --copy-contents fifo fifo2
   232	    //
   233	    // causes `fifo2` to be created with limited permissions (mode 622
   234	    // or maybe 600 it seems), and then after `fifo` is closed, the
   235	    // permissions get updated to match those of `fifo`. This doesn't
   236	    // make much sense to me but the behavior appears in
   237	    // `tests/cp/file-perm-race.sh`.
   238	    //
   239	    // So it seems that if `--preserve=ownership` is true then what we
   240	    // need to do is create the destination file with limited
   241	    // permissions, copy the contents, then update the permissions. If
   242	    // `--preserve=ownership` is not true, however, then we can just
   243	    // match the mode of the source file.
   244	    //
   245	    // TODO Update the code below to respect the case where
   246	    // `--preserve=ownership` is not true.
   247	    let mut src_file = File::open(&source)?;
   248	    let mode = 0o622 & !get_umask();
   249	    let mut dst_file = OpenOptions::new()
   250	        .create(true)
   251	        .write(true)
   252	        .mode(mode)
   253	        .open(&dest)?;
   254	
   255	    let num_bytes_copied = buf_copy::copy_stream(&mut src_file, &mut dst_file)
   256	        .map_err(|_| std::io::Error::from(std::io::ErrorKind::Other))?;
   257	
   258	    if is_fifo {
   259	        dst_file.set_permissions(src_file.metadata()?.permissions())?;
   260	    }
   261	
   262	    Ok(num_bytes_copied)
   263	}
   264	
   265	/// Copies `source` to `dest` using copy-on-write if possible.
   266	///
   267	/// The `source_is_fifo` flag must be set to `true` if and only if
   268	/// `source` is a FIFO (also known as a named pipe). In this case,
   269	/// copy-on-write is not possible, so we copy the contents using
   270	/// [`std::io::copy`].
   271	pub(crate) fn copy_on_write(
   272	    source: &Path,
   273	    dest: &Path,
   274	    reflink_mode: ReflinkMode,
   275	    sparse_mode: SparseMode,
   276	    context: &str,
   277	    source_is_fifo: bool,
   278	    source_is_stream: bool,
   279	) -> CopyResult<CopyDebug> {
   280	    let mut copy_debug = CopyDebug {
   281	        offload: OffloadReflinkDebug::Unknown,
   282	        reflink: OffloadReflinkDebug::Unsupported,
   283	        sparse_detection: SparseDebug::No,
   284	    };
   285	    let result = match (reflink_mode, sparse_mode) {
   286	        (ReflinkMode::Never, SparseMode::Always) => {
   287	            copy_debug.sparse_detection = SparseDebug::Zeros;
   288	            // Default SparseDebug val for SparseMode::Always
   289	            copy_debug.reflink = OffloadReflinkDebug::No;
   290	            if source_is_stream {
   291	                copy_debug.offload = OffloadReflinkDebug::Avoided;
   292	                copy_stream(source, dest, source_is_fifo).map(|_| ())
   293	            } else {
   294	                let mut copy_method = CopyMethod::Default;
   295	                let result = handle_reflink_never_sparse_always(source, dest);
   296	                if let Ok((debug, method)) = result {
   297	                    copy_debug = debug;
   298	                    copy_method = method;
   299	                }
   300	
   301	                match copy_method {
   302	                    CopyMethod::FSCopy => std::fs::copy(source, dest).map(|_| ()),
   303	                    _ => sparse_copy(source, dest),
   304	                }
   305	            }
   306	        }
   307	        (ReflinkMode::Never, SparseMode::Never) => {
   308	            copy_debug.reflink = OffloadReflinkDebug::No;
   309	
   310	            if source_is_stream {
   311	                copy_debug.offload = OffloadReflinkDebug::Avoided;
   312	                copy_stream(source, dest, source_is_fifo).map(|_| ())
   313	            } else {
   314	                let result = handle_reflink_never_sparse_never(source);
   315	                if let Ok(debug) = result {
   316	                    copy_debug = debug;
   317	                }
   318	                std::fs::copy(source, dest).map(|_| ())
   319	            }
   320	        }
   321	        (ReflinkMode::Never, SparseMode::Auto) => {
   322	            copy_debug.reflink = OffloadReflinkDebug::No;
   323	
   324	            if source_is_stream {
   325	                copy_debug.offload = OffloadReflinkDebug::Avoided;
   326	                copy_stream(source, dest, source_is_fifo).map(|_| ())
   327	            } else {
   328	                let mut copy_method = CopyMethod::Default;
   329	                let result = handle_reflink_never_sparse_auto(source, dest);
   330	                if let Ok((debug, method)) = result {
   331	                    copy_debug = debug;
   332	                    copy_method = method;
   333	                }
   334	
   335	                match copy_method {
   336	                    CopyMethod::SparseCopyWithoutHole => sparse_copy_without_hole(source, dest),
   337	                    _ => std::fs::copy(source, dest).map(|_| ()),
   338	                }
   339	            }
   340	        }
   341	        (ReflinkMode::Auto, SparseMode::Always) => {
   342	            copy_debug.sparse_detection = SparseDebug::Zeros; // Default SparseDebug val for
   343	            // SparseMode::Always
   344	            if source_is_stream {
   345	                copy_debug.offload = OffloadReflinkDebug::Avoided;
   346	                copy_stream(source, dest, source_is_fifo).map(|_| ())
   347	            } else {
   348	                let mut copy_method = CopyMethod::Default;
   349	                let result = handle_reflink_auto_sparse_always(source, dest);
   350	                if let Ok((debug, method)) = result {
   351	                    copy_debug = debug;
   352	                    copy_method = method;
   353	                }
   354	
   355	                match copy_method {
   356	                    CopyMethod::FSCopy => clone(source, dest, CloneFallback::FSCopy),
   357	                    _ => clone(source, dest, CloneFallback::SparseCopy),
   358	                }
   359	            }
   360	        }
   361	
   362	        (ReflinkMode::Auto, SparseMode::Never) => {
   363	            copy_debug.reflink = OffloadReflinkDebug::No;
   364	            if source_is_stream {
   365	                copy_debug.offload = OffloadReflinkDebug::Avoided;
   366	                copy_stream(source, dest, source_is_fifo).map(|_| ())
   367	            } else {
   368	                let result = handle_reflink_auto_sparse_never(source);
   369	                if let Ok(debug) = result {
   370	                    copy_debug = debug;
   371	                }
   372	
   373	                clone(source, dest, CloneFallback::FSCopy)
   374	            }
   375	        }
   376	        (ReflinkMode::Auto, SparseMode::Auto) => {
   377	            if source_is_stream {
   378	                copy_debug.offload = OffloadReflinkDebug::Unsupported;
   379	                copy_stream(source, dest, source_is_fifo).map(|_| ())
   380	            } else {
   381	                let mut copy_method = CopyMethod::Default;
   382	                let result = handle_reflink_auto_sparse_auto(source, dest);
   383	                if let Ok((debug, method)) = result {
   384	                    copy_debug = debug;
   385	                    copy_method = method;
   386	                }
   387	
   388	                match copy_method {
   389	                    CopyMethod::SparseCopyWithoutHole => {
   390	                        clone(source, dest, CloneFallback::SparseCopyWithoutHole)
   391	                    }
   392	                    _ => clone(source, dest, CloneFallback::FSCopy),
   393	                }
   394	            }
   395	        }
   396	
   397	        (ReflinkMode::Always, SparseMode::Auto) => {
   398	            copy_debug.sparse_detection = SparseDebug::No;
   399	            copy_debug.reflink = OffloadReflinkDebug::Yes;
   400	
   401	            clone(source, dest, CloneFallback::Error)
   402	        }
   403	        (ReflinkMode::Always, _) => {
   404	            return Err(get_message("cp-error-reflink-always-sparse-auto").into());
   405	        }
   406	    };
   407	    result.map_err(|e| CpError::IoErrContext(e, context.to_owned()))?;
   408	    Ok(copy_debug)
   409	}
   410	
   411	/// Handles debug results when flags are "--reflink=auto" and "--sparse=always" and specifies what
   412	/// type of copy should be used
   413	fn handle_reflink_auto_sparse_always(
   414	    source: &Path,
   415	    dest: &Path,
   416	) -> Result<(CopyDebug, CopyMethod), std::io::Error> {
   417	    let mut copy_debug = CopyDebug {

   423	    let (data_flag, size, blocks) = check_for_data(source)?;
   424	    let sparse_flag = check_sparse_detection(source)?;
   425	
   426	    if data_flag || size < 512 {
   427	        copy_debug.offload = OffloadReflinkDebug::Avoided;

     2	//
     3	// For the full copyright and license information, please view the LICENSE

     5	// spell-checker:ignore reflink
     6	use std::fs;
     7	use std::path::Path;
     8	use uucore::locale::get_message;
     9	
    10	use crate::{
    11	    CopyDebug, CopyResult, CpError, OffloadReflinkDebug, ReflinkMode, SparseDebug, SparseMode,
    12	};
    13	
    14	/// Copies `source` to `dest` for systems without copy-on-write
    15	pub(crate) fn copy_on_write(
    16	    source: &Path,
    17	    dest: &Path,
    18	    reflink_mode: ReflinkMode,
    19	    sparse_mode: SparseMode,
    20	    context: &str,
    21	) -> CopyResult<CopyDebug> {
    22	    if reflink_mode != ReflinkMode::Never {
    23	        return Err(get_message("cp-error-reflink-not-supported")
    24	            .to_string()
    25	            .into());
    26	    }
    27	    if sparse_mode != SparseMode::Auto {
    28	        return Err(get_message("cp-error-sparse-not-supported")
    29	            .to_string()
    30	            .into());
    31	    }
    32	    let copy_debug = CopyDebug {
    33	        offload: OffloadReflinkDebug::Unsupported,
    34	        reflink: OffloadReflinkDebug::Unsupported,
    35	        sparse_detection: SparseDebug::Unsupported,
    36	    };
    37	    fs::copy(source, dest).map_err(|e| CpError::IoErrContext(e, context.to_owned()))?;
    38	
    39	    Ok(copy_debug)
    40	}
    41

set -e

# Build the cp tool first
cd /testbed/repo
cargo build --release 2>&1 | tail -5

CP_BIN="/testbed/repo/target/release/coreutils"

# Create a temporary directory for testing
TEST_DIR=$(mktemp -d)
cd "$TEST_DIR"

# Create test files
echo "This is a longer text that we will write first" > original.txt
echo "Short" > short.txt

# Copy the original file to target using uutils cp
$CP_BIN cp original.txt target.txt

echo "=== Initial copy ==="
echo "Target content:"
cat target.txt
echo ""
echo "Target size: $(wc -c < target.txt) bytes"

# Now copy the shorter file to the same target
$CP_BIN cp short.txt target.txt

echo ""
echo "=== After copying shorter file ==="
echo "Target content:"
cat target.txt
echo ""
echo "Target size: $(wc -c < target.txt) bytes"
echo "Expected size: $(wc -c < short.txt) bytes"

# Check if the issue exists
EXPECTED_SIZE=$(wc -c < short.txt)
ACTUAL_SIZE=$(wc -c < target.txt)

if [ "$EXPECTED_SIZE" -ne "$ACTUAL_SIZE" ]; then
    echo ""
    echo "BUG CONFIRMED: File was not properly truncated!"
    echo "Expected size: $EXPECTED_SIZE, Actual size: $ACTUAL_SIZE"
    exit 1
else
    echo ""
    echo "No bug detected - file was properly truncated"
    exit 0
fi
'

    echo "BUG CONFIRMED: File was not properly truncated!"
    echo "Expected size: $EXPECTED_SIZE, Actual size: $ACTUAL_SIZE"
    echo "Hex dump of target.txt:"
    hexdump -C target.txt
    exit 1
else
    echo ""
    echo "No bug detected - file was properly truncated"
    exit 0
fi

   224	/// determine if we need to modify the file's attributes before and after copying.
   225	fn copy_stream<P>(source: P, dest: P, is_fifo: bool) -> std::io::Result<u64>
   226	where
   227	    P: AsRef<Path>,
   228	{
   229	    // For some reason,
   230	    //
   231	    //     cp --preserve=ownership --copy-contents fifo fifo2
   232	    //
   233	    // causes `fifo2` to be created with limited permissions (mode 622
   234	    // or maybe 600 it seems), and then after `fifo` is closed, the
   235	    // permissions get updated to match those of `fifo`. This doesn't
   236	    // make much sense to me but the behavior appears in
   237	    // `tests/cp/file-perm-race.sh`.
   238	    //
   239	    // So it seems that if `--preserve=ownership` is true then what we
   240	    // need to do is create the destination file with limited
   241	    // permissions, copy the contents, then update the permissions. If
   242	    // `--preserve=ownership` is not true, however, then we can just
   243	    // match the mode of the source file.
   244	    //
   245	    // TODO Update the code below to respect the case where
   246	    // `--preserve=ownership` is not true.
   247	    let mut src_file = File::open(&source)?;
   248	    let mode = 0o622 & !get_umask();
   249	    let mut dst_file = OpenOptions::new()
   250	        .create(true)
   251	        .write(true)
   252	        .mode(mode)
   253	        .open(&dest)?;
   254	
   255	    let num_bytes_copied = buf_copy::copy_stream(&mut src_file, &mut dst_file)
   256	        .map_err(|_| std::io::Error::from(std::io::ErrorKind::Other))?;
   257	
   258	    if is_fifo {
   259	        dst_file.set_permissions(src_file.metadata()?.permissions())?;
   260	    }
   261	
   262	    Ok(num_bytes_copied)
   263	}

   130	fn sparse_copy_without_hole<P>(source: P, dest: P) -> std::io::Result<()>
   131	where
   132	    P: AsRef<Path>,
   133	{
   134	    let src_file = File::open(source)?;
   135	    let dst_file = File::create(dest)?;
   136	    let dst_fd = dst_file.as_raw_fd();
   137	
   138	    let size = src_file.metadata()?.size();
   139	    if unsafe { libc::ftruncate(dst_fd, size.try_into().unwrap()) } < 0 {
   140	        return Err(std::io::Error::last_os_error());
   141	    }
   142	    let src_fd = src_file.as_raw_fd();
   143	    let mut current_offset: isize = 0;
   144	    // Maximize the data read at once to 16 MiB to avoid memory hogging with large files
   145	    // 16 MiB chunks should saturate an SSD
   146	    let step = std::cmp::min(size, 16 * 1024 * 1024) as usize;
   147	    let mut buf: Vec<u8> = vec![0x0; step];
   148	    loop {
   149	        let result = unsafe { libc::lseek(src_fd, current_offset.try_into().unwrap(), SEEK_DATA) }
   150	            .try_into()
   151	            .unwrap();
   152	
   153	        current_offset = result;
   154	        let hole: isize =
   155	            unsafe { libc::lseek(src_fd, current_offset.try_into().unwrap(), SEEK_HOLE) }
   156	                .try_into()
   157	                .unwrap();
   158	        if result == -1 || hole == -1 {
   159	            break;
   160	        }
   161	        if result <= -2 || hole <= -2 {
   162	            return Err(std::io::Error::last_os_error());
   163	        }
   164	        let len: isize = hole - current_offset;
   165	        // Read and write data in chunks of `step` while reusing the same buffer
   166	        for i in (0..len).step_by(step) {
   167	            // Ensure we don't read past the end of the file or the start of the next hole
   168	            let read_len = std::cmp::min((len - i) as usize, step);
   169	            let buf = &mut buf[..read_len];
   170	            src_file.read_exact_at(buf, (current_offset + i) as u64)?;
   171	            dst_file.write_all_at(buf, (current_offset + i) as u64)?;
   172	        }
   173	        current_offset = hole;
   174	    }
   175	    Ok(())
   176	}

   177	/// Perform a sparse copy from one file to another.
   178	/// Creates a holes for large sequences of zeros in non_sparse_files, used for --sparse=always
   179	#[cfg(any(target_os = "linux", target_os = "android"))]
   180	fn sparse_copy<P>(source: P, dest: P) -> std::io::Result<()>
   181	where
   182	    P: AsRef<Path>,
   183	{
   184	    let mut src_file = File::open(source)?;
   185	    let dst_file = File::create(dest)?;
   186	    let dst_fd = dst_file.as_raw_fd();
   187	
   188	    let size: usize = src_file.metadata()?.size().try_into().unwrap();
   189	    if unsafe { libc::ftruncate(dst_fd, size.try_into().unwrap()) } < 0 {
   190	        return Err(std::io::Error::last_os_error());
   191	    }
   192	
   193	    let blksize = dst_file.metadata()?.blksize();
   194	    let mut buf: Vec<u8> = vec![0; blksize.try_into().unwrap()];
   195	    let mut current_offset: usize = 0;
   196	
   197	    // TODO Perhaps we can employ the "fiemap ioctl" API to get the
   198	    // file extent mappings:
   199	    // https://www.kernel.org/doc/html/latest/filesystems/fiemap.html
   200	    while current_offset < size {
   201	        let this_read = src_file.read(&mut buf)?;
   202	        let buf = &buf[..this_read];
   203	        if buf.iter().any(|&x| x != 0) {
   204	            dst_file.write_all_at(buf, current_offset.try_into().unwrap())?;
   205	        }
   206	        current_offset += this_read;
   207	    }
   208	    Ok(())
   209	}

    52	/// Use the Linux `ioctl_ficlone` API to do a copy-on-write clone.
    53	///
    54	/// `fallback` controls what to do if the system call fails.
    55	#[cfg(any(target_os = "linux", target_os = "android"))]
    56	fn clone<P>(source: P, dest: P, fallback: CloneFallback) -> std::io::Result<()>
    57	where
    58	    P: AsRef<Path>,
    59	{
    60	    let src_file = File::open(&source)?;
    61	    let dst_file = File::create(&dest)?;
    62	    let src_fd = src_file.as_raw_fd();
    63	    let dst_fd = dst_file.as_raw_fd();
    64	    // Using .try_into().unwrap() is required as glibc, musl & android all have different type for ioctl()
    65	    #[allow(clippy::unnecessary_fallible_conversions)]
    66	    let result = unsafe {
    67	        libc::ioctl(
    68	            dst_fd,
    69	            linux_raw_sys::ioctl::FICLONE.try_into().unwrap(),
    70	            src_fd,
    71	        )
    72	    };
    73	    if result == 0 {
    74	        return Ok(());
    75	    }
    76	    match fallback {
    77	        CloneFallback::Error => Err(std::io::Error::last_os_error()),
    78	        CloneFallback::FSCopy => std::fs::copy(source, dest).map(|_| ()),
    79	        CloneFallback::SparseCopy => sparse_copy(source, dest),
    80	        CloneFallback::SparseCopyWithoutHole => sparse_copy_without_hole(source, dest),
    81	    }
    82	}

    fs::create_dir_all(&dir).unwrap();

Good! So `std::fs::copy` properly truncates files. The problem is in the `copy_stream` function. Let me now create a test that reproduces the issue when copying from a stream/FIFO/character device:

🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor create /testbed/reproduce_stream_issue.sh --file_text '#!/bin/bash

CP_BIN="/testbed/repo/target/debug/coreutils"

# Create a temporary directory for testing
TEST_DIR=$(mktemp -d)
cd "$TEST_DIR"

echo "Test directory: $TEST_DIR"

# Create a named pipe (FIFO)
mkfifo source_fifo

# First, write long content through the pipe and copy it
(echo "This is a longer text that we will write first" > source_fifo) &
$CP_BIN cp --copy-contents source_fifo target.txt

echo "=== Initial copy from FIFO ==="
echo "Target content:"
cat target.txt
echo ""
echo "Target size: $(wc -c < target.txt) bytes"

# Now write shorter content through the pipe and copy it
(echo "Short" > source_fifo) &
$CP_BIN cp --copy-contents source_fifo target.txt

echo ""
echo "=== After copying shorter content from FIFO ==="
echo "Target content:"
cat target.txt
echo ""
echo "Target size: $(wc -c < target.txt) bytes"
echo "Expected: '"'"'Short'"'"' followed by newline = 6 bytes"

# Check if the issue exists
EXPECTED_SIZE=6  # "Short\n"
ACTUAL_SIZE=$(wc -c < target.txt)

if [ "$EXPECTED_SIZE" -ne "$ACTUAL_SIZE" ]; then
    echo ""
    echo "BUG CONFIRMED: File was not properly truncated when copying from FIFO!"
    echo "Expected size: $EXPECTED_SIZE, Actual size: $ACTUAL_SIZE"
    echo "Hex dump of target.txt:"
    hexdump -C target.txt
    rm -rf "$TEST_DIR"
    exit 1
else
    echo ""
    echo "No bug detected - file was properly truncated"
    rm -rf "$TEST_DIR"
    exit 0
fi
'

Ah! `/dev/stdin` is a **character special file** (char device). So when you copy from `/dev/stdin`, it takes the `copy_stream` path which doesn't truncate the destination file! Let me create a better test:

🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor create /testbed/reproduce_char_device.sh --file_text '#!/bin/bash

CP_BIN="/testbed/repo/target/debug/coreutils"

# Create a temporary directory for testing
TEST_DIR=$(mktemp -d)
cd "$TEST_DIR"

echo "Test directory: $TEST_DIR"

# First, copy long content from a character device (/dev/stdin)
echo "This is a longer text that we will write first" | $CP_BIN cp /dev/stdin target.txt

echo "=== Initial copy from /dev/stdin (char device) ==="
echo "Target content:"
cat target.txt
echo ""
echo "Target size: $(wc -c < target.txt) bytes"

# Now copy shorter content from /dev/stdin
echo "Short" | $CP_BIN cp /dev/stdin target.txt

echo ""
echo "=== After copying shorter content from /dev/stdin ==="
echo "Target content:"
cat target.txt
echo ""
echo "Target size: $(wc -c < target.txt) bytes"
echo "Expected: '"'"'Short'"'"' followed by newline = 6 bytes"

# Check if the issue exists
EXPECTED_SIZE=6  # "Short\n"
ACTUAL_SIZE=$(wc -c < target.txt)

if [ "$EXPECTED_SIZE" -ne "$ACTUAL_SIZE" ]; then
    echo ""
    echo "BUG CONFIRMED: File was not properly truncated when copying from character device!"
    echo "Expected size: $EXPECTED_SIZE, Actual size: $ACTUAL_SIZE"
    echo "Hex dump of target.txt:"
    hexdump -C target.txt
    rm -rf "$TEST_DIR"
    exit 1
else
    echo ""
    echo "No bug detected - file was properly truncated"
    rm -rf "$TEST_DIR"
    exit 0
fi
'

  1943	fn handle_existing_dest(
  1944	    source: &Path,
  1945	    dest: &Path,
  1946	    options: &Options,
  1947	    source_in_command_line: bool,
  1948	    copied_files: &HashMap<FileInformation, PathBuf>,
  1949	) -> CopyResult<()> {
  1950	    // Disallow copying a file to itself, unless `--force` and
  1951	    // `--backup` are both specified.
  1952	    if is_forbidden_to_copy_to_same_file(source, dest, options, source_in_command_line) {
  1953	        return Err(get_message_with_args(
  1954	            "cp-error-same-file",
  1955	            HashMap::from([
  1956	                ("source".to_string(), source.quote().to_string()),
  1957	                ("dest".to_string(), dest.quote().to_string()),
  1958	            ]),
  1959	        )
  1960	        .into());
  1961	    }
  1962	
  1963	    if options.update == UpdateMode::None {
  1964	        if options.debug {
  1965	            println!("skipped {}", dest.quote());
  1966	        }
  1967	        return Err(CpError::Skipped(false));
  1968	    }
  1969	
  1970	    if options.update != UpdateMode::IfOlder {
  1971	        options.overwrite.verify(dest, options.debug)?;
  1972	    }
  1973	
  1974	    let mut is_dest_removed = false;
  1975	    let backup_path = backup_control::get_backup_path(options.backup, dest, &options.backup_suffix);
  1976	    if let Some(backup_path) = backup_path {
  1977	        if paths_refer_to_same_file(source, &backup_path, true) {
  1978	            return Err(get_message_with_args(
  1979	                "cp-error-backing-up-destroy-source",
  1980	                HashMap::from([
  1981	                    ("dest".to_string(), dest.quote().to_string()),
  1982	                    ("source".to_string(), source.quote().to_string()),
  1983	                ]),
  1984	            )
  1985	            .into());
  1986	        }
  1987	        is_dest_removed = dest.is_symlink();
  1988	        backup_dest(dest, &backup_path, is_dest_removed)?;
  1989	    }
  1990	    if !is_dest_removed {
  1991	        delete_dest_if_needed_and_allowed(
  1992	            source,
  1993	            dest,
  1994	            options,
  1995	            source_in_command_line,
  1996	            copied_files,
  1997	        )?;
  1998	    }
  1999	
  2000	    Ok(())
  2001	}
  2002	
  2003	/// Checks if:
  2004	/// * `dest` needs to be deleted before the copy operation can proceed
  2005	/// * the provided options allow this deletion
  2006	///
  2007	/// If so, deletes `dest`.
  2008	fn delete_dest_if_needed_and_allowed(
  2009	    source: &Path,
  2010	    dest: &Path,
  2011	    options: &Options,
  2012	    source_in_command_line: bool,
  2013	    copied_files: &HashMap<FileInformation, PathBuf>,
  2014	) -> CopyResult<()> {
  2015	    let delete_dest = match options.overwrite {
  2016	        OverwriteMode::Clobber(cl) | OverwriteMode::Interactive(cl) => {
  2017	            match cl {
  2018	                // FIXME: print that the file was removed if --verbose is enabled
  2019	                ClobberMode::Force => {
  2020	                    // TODO
  2021	                    // Using `readonly` here to check if `dest` needs to be deleted is not correct:
  2022	                    // "On Unix-based platforms this checks if any of the owner, group or others write permission bits are set. It does not check if the current user is in the file's assigned group. It also does not check ACLs. Therefore the return value of this function cannot be relied upon to predict whether attempts to read or write the file will actually succeed."
  2023	                    // This results in some copy operations failing, because this necessary deletion is being skipped.
  2024	                    is_symlink_loop(dest) || fs::metadata(dest)?.permissions().readonly()
  2025	                }
  2026	                ClobberMode::RemoveDestination => true,
  2027	                ClobberMode::Standard => {
  2028	                    // Consider the following files:
  2029	                    //
  2030	                    // * `src/f` - a regular file
  2031	                    // * `src/link` - a hard link to `src/f`
  2032	                    // * `dest/src/f` - a different regular file
  2033	                    //
  2034	                    // In this scenario, if we do `cp -a src/ dest/`, it is
  2035	                    // possible that the order of traversal causes `src/link`
  2036	                    // to get copied first (to `dest/src/link`). In that case,
  2037	                    // in order to make sure `dest/src/link` is a hard link to
  2038	                    // `dest/src/f` and `dest/src/f` has the contents of
  2039	                    // `src/f`, we delete the existing file to allow the hard
  2040	                    // linking.
  2041	                    options.preserve_hard_links() &&
  2042	                            // only try to remove dest file only if the current source
  2043	                            // is hardlink to a file that is already copied
  2044	                            copied_files.contains_key(
  2045	                                &FileInformation::from_path(
  2046	                                    source,
  2047	                                    options.dereference(source_in_command_line)
  2048	                                ).map_err(|e| CpError::IoErrContext(e, format!("cannot stat {}", source.quote())))?
  2049	                            )
  2050	                }
  2051	            }
  2052	        }
  2053	        OverwriteMode::NoClobber => false,
  2054	    };
  2055	
  2056	    if delete_dest {
  2057	        fs::remove_file(dest)?;
  2058	    }
  2059	
  2060	    Ok(())

fn main() {
    let path = "/tmp/test_open.txt";
    
    // Create file with long content
    {
        let mut f = File::create(path).unwrap();
        f.write_all(b"This is a longer text that we will write first").unwrap();
    }
    
    println!("Initial size: {}", std::fs::metadata(path).unwrap().len());
    println!("Initial content: {:?}", std::fs::read_to_string(path).unwrap());

#!/bin/bash

CP_BIN="/testbed/repo/target/debug/coreutils"

     1	// This file is part of the uutils coreutils package.
     2	//
     3	// For the full copyright and license information, please view the LICENSE
     4	// file that was distributed with this source code.
     5	
     6	//! This module provides several buffer-based copy/write functions that leverage
     7	//! the `splice` system call in Linux systems, thus increasing the I/O
     8	//! performance of copying between two file descriptors. This module is mostly
     9	//! used by utilities to work around the limitations of Rust's `fs::copy` which
    10	//! does not handle copying special files (e.g pipes, character/block devices).
    11	
    12	pub mod common;
    13	
    14	#[cfg(any(target_os = "linux", target_os = "android"))]
    15	pub mod linux;
    16	#[cfg(any(target_os = "linux", target_os = "android"))]
    17	pub use linux::*;
    18	
    19	#[cfg(not(any(target_os = "linux", target_os = "android")))]
    20	pub mod other;
    21	#[cfg(not(any(target_os = "linux", target_os = "android")))]
    22	pub use other::copy_stream;
    23	
    24	#[cfg(test)]
    25	mod tests {
    26	    use super::*;
    27	    use std::fs::File;
    28	    use tempfile::tempdir;
    29	
    30	    #[cfg(unix)]
    31	    use {
    32	        crate::pipes,
    33	        std::fs::OpenOptions,
    34	        std::{
    35	            io::{Seek, SeekFrom},
    36	            thread,
    37	        },
    38	    };
    39	
    40	    use std::io::{Read, Write};
    41	
    42	    #[cfg(unix)]
    43	    fn new_temp_file() -> File {
    44	        let temp_dir = tempdir().unwrap();
    45	        OpenOptions::new()
    46	            .read(true)
    47	            .write(true)
    48	            .create(true)
    49	            .truncate(true)
    50	            .open(temp_dir.path().join("file.txt"))
    51	            .unwrap()
    52	    }
    53	
    54	    #[cfg(any(target_os = "linux", target_os = "android"))]
    55	    #[test]
    56	    fn test_copy_exact() {
    57	        let (mut pipe_read, mut pipe_write) = pipes::pipe().unwrap();
    58	        let data = b"Hello, world!";
    59	        let n = pipe_write.write(data).unwrap();
    60	        assert_eq!(n, data.len());
    61	        let mut buf = [0; 1024];
    62	        let n = copy_exact(&pipe_read, &pipe_write, data.len()).unwrap();
    63	        let n2 = pipe_read.read(&mut buf).unwrap();
    64	        assert_eq!(n, n2);
    65	        assert_eq!(&buf[..n], data);
    66	    }
    67	
    68	    #[test]
    69	    #[cfg(unix)]
    70	    fn test_copy_stream() {
    71	        let mut dest_file = new_temp_file();
    72	
    73	        let (mut pipe_read, mut pipe_write) = pipes::pipe().unwrap();
    74	        let data = b"Hello, world!";
    75	        let thread = thread::spawn(move || {
    76	            pipe_write.write_all(data).unwrap();
    77	        });
    78	        let result = copy_stream(&mut pipe_read, &mut dest_file).unwrap();
    79	        thread.join().unwrap();
    80	        assert_eq!(result, data.len() as u64);
    81	
    82	        // We would have been at the end already, so seek again to the start.
    83	        dest_file.seek(SeekFrom::Start(0)).unwrap();
    84	
    85	        let mut buf = Vec::new();
    86	        dest_file.read_to_end(&mut buf).unwrap();
    87	
    88	        assert_eq!(buf, data);
    89	    }
    90	
    91	    #[test]
    92	    #[cfg(not(unix))]
    93	    // Test for non-unix platforms. We use regular files instead.
    94	    fn test_copy_stream() {
    95	        let temp_dir = tempdir().unwrap();
    96	        let src_path = temp_dir.path().join("src.txt");
    97	        let dest_path = temp_dir.path().join("dest.txt");
    98	
    99	        let mut src_file = File::create(&src_path).unwrap();
   100	        let mut dest_file = File::create(&dest_path).unwrap();
   101	
   102	        let data = b"Hello, world!";
   103	        src_file.write_all(data).unwrap();
   104	        src_file.sync_all().unwrap();
   105	
   106	        let mut src_file = File::open(&src_path).unwrap();
   107	        let bytes_copied = copy_stream(&mut src_file, &mut dest_file).unwrap();
   108	
   109	        let mut dest_file = File::open(&dest_path).unwrap();
   110	        let mut buf = Vec::new();
   111	        dest_file.read_to_end(&mut buf).unwrap();
   112	
   113	        assert_eq!(bytes_copied as usize, data.len());
   114	        assert_eq!(buf, data);
   115	    }
   116	}

     1	// This file is part of the uutils coreutils package.
     2	//
     3	// For the full copyright and license information, please view the LICENSE
     4	// file that was distributed with this source code.
     5	
     6	//! Buffer-based copying implementation for Linux and Android.
     7	
     8	use crate::{
     9	    error::UResult,
    10	    pipes::{pipe, splice, splice_exact},
    11	};
    12	
    13	/// Buffer-based copying utilities for unix (excluding Linux).
    14	use std::{
    15	    io::{Read, Write},
    16	    os::fd::{AsFd, AsRawFd},
    17	};
    18	
    19	use super::common::Error;
    20	
    21	/// A readable file descriptor.
    22	pub trait FdReadable: Read + AsRawFd + AsFd {}
    23	
    24	impl<T> FdReadable for T where T: Read + AsFd + AsRawFd {}
    25	
    26	/// A writable file descriptor.
    27	pub trait FdWritable: Write + AsFd + AsRawFd {}
    28	
    29	impl<T> FdWritable for T where T: Write + AsFd + AsRawFd {}
    30	
    31	const SPLICE_SIZE: usize = 1024 * 128;
    32	const BUF_SIZE: usize = 1024 * 16;
    33	
    34	/// Conversion from a `nix::Error` into our `Error` which implements `UError`.
    35	impl From<nix::Error> for Error {
    36	    fn from(error: nix::Error) -> Self {
    37	        Self::Io(std::io::Error::from_raw_os_error(error as i32))
    38	    }
    39	}
    40	
    41	/// Copy data from `Read` implementor `source` into a `Write` implementor
    42	/// `dest`. This works by reading a chunk of data from `source` and writing the
    43	/// data to `dest` in a loop.
    44	///
    45	/// This function uses the Linux-specific `splice` call when possible which does
    46	/// not use any intermediate user-space buffer. It falls backs to
    47	/// `std::io::copy` when the call fails and is still recoverable.
    48	///
    49	/// # Arguments
    50	/// * `source` - `Read` implementor to copy data from.
    51	/// * `dest` - `Write` implementor to copy data to.
    52	///
    53	/// # Returns
    54	///
    55	/// Result of operation and bytes successfully written (as a `u64`) when
    56	/// operation is successful.
    57	pub fn copy_stream<R, S>(src: &mut R, dest: &mut S) -> UResult<u64>
    58	where
    59	    R: Read + AsFd + AsRawFd,
    60	    S: Write + AsFd + AsRawFd,
    61	{
    62	    // If we're on Linux or Android, try to use the splice() system call
    63	    // for faster writing. If it works, we're done.
    64	    let result = splice_write(src, &dest.as_fd())?;
    65	    if !result.1 {
    66	        return Ok(result.0);
    67	    }
    68	
    69	    // If the splice() call failed, fall back on slower writing.
    70	    let result = std::io::copy(src, dest)?;
    71	
    72	    // If the splice() call failed and there has been some data written to
    73	    // stdout via while loop above AND there will be second splice() call
    74	    // that will succeed, data pushed through splice will be output before
    75	    // the data buffered in stdout.lock. Therefore additional explicit flush
    76	    // is required here.
    77	    dest.flush()?;
    78	    Ok(result)
    79	}
    80	
    81	/// Write from source `handle` into destination `write_fd` using Linux-specific
    82	/// `splice` system call.
    83	///
    84	/// # Arguments
    85	/// - `source` - source handle
    86	/// - `dest` - destination handle
    87	#[inline]
    88	pub(crate) fn splice_write<R, S>(source: &R, dest: &S) -> UResult<(u64, bool)>
    89	where
    90	    R: Read + AsFd + AsRawFd,
    91	    S: AsRawFd + AsFd,
    92	{
    93	    let (pipe_rd, pipe_wr) = pipe()?;
    94	    let mut bytes: u64 = 0;
    95	
    96	    loop {
    97	        match splice(&source, &pipe_wr, SPLICE_SIZE) {
    98	            Ok(n) => {
    99	                if n == 0 {
   100	                    return Ok((bytes, false));
   101	                }
   102	                if splice_exact(&pipe_rd, dest, n).is_err() {
   103	                    // If the first splice manages to copy to the intermediate
   104	                    // pipe, but the second splice to stdout fails for some reason
   105	                    // we can recover by copying the data that we have from the
   106	                    // intermediate pipe to stdout using normal read/write. Then
   107	                    // we tell the caller to fall back.
   108	                    copy_exact(&pipe_rd, dest, n)?;
   109	                    return Ok((bytes, true));
   110	                }
   111	
   112	                bytes += n as u64;
   113	            }
   114	            Err(_) => {
   115	                return Ok((bytes, true));
   116	            }
   117	        }
   118	    }
   119	}
   120	
   121	/// Move exactly `num_bytes` bytes from `read_fd` to `write_fd` using the `read`
   122	/// and `write` calls.
   123	#[cfg(any(target_os = "linux", target_os = "android"))]
   124	pub(crate) fn copy_exact(
   125	    read_fd: &impl AsFd,
   126	    write_fd: &impl AsFd,
   127	    num_bytes: usize,
   128	) -> std::io::Result<usize> {
   129	    use nix::unistd;
   130	
   131	    let mut left = num_bytes;
   132	    let mut buf = [0; BUF_SIZE];
   133	    let mut written = 0;
   134	    while left > 0 {
   135	        let read = unistd::read(read_fd, &mut buf)?;
   136	        assert_ne!(read, 0, "unexpected end of pipe");
   137	        while written < read {
   138	            let n = unistd::write(write_fd, &buf[written..read])?;
   139	            written += n;
   140	        }
   141	        left -= read;
   142	    }
   143	    Ok(written)
   144	}
   145

cat > /tmp/test_exact_scenario.sh << 'EOF'
#!/bin/bash

# Simulate wl-paste scenario more closely
# We'll use a FIFO to simulate real-time pipe input

TEST_DIR=$(mktemp -d)
cd "$TEST_DIR"

mkfifo pipe

# Create pre-existing file with long content
echo "This is a longer text that we will write first with more data to make it obvious" > tmp

echo "=== Initial file ==="
cat tmp
echo ""
echo "Size: $(wc -c < tmp) bytes"

# Simulate first clipboard event
(echo "First clipboard content that is somewhat long" > pipe) &
/bin/cp pipe tmp

echo ""
echo "=== After first clipboard event ==="
cat tmp
echo "Size: $(wc -c < tmp) bytes"

# Simulate second clipboard event with shorter content  
(echo "Short" > pipe) &
/bin/cp pipe tmp

echo ""
echo "=== After second clipboard event (shorter) ==="
cat tmp
echo "Size: $(wc -c < tmp) bytes"
echo "Expected: 6 bytes"

# Check result
EXPECTED_SIZE=6
ACTUAL_SIZE=$(wc -c < tmp)

if [ "$EXPECTED_SIZE" -ne "$ACTUAL_SIZE" ]; then
    echo "BUG: File was not properly truncated!"
    echo "Content in hex:"
    od -c tmp
else
    echo "OK: File was properly truncated"
fi

rm -rf "$TEST_DIR"
EOF
chmod +x /tmp/test_exact_scenario.sh && /tmp/test_exact_scenario.sh

So for FIFOs, if it's recursive and not copy_contents, it calls copy_fifo which just creates a new FIFO. Otherwise, it calls copy_on_write with source_is_fifo=true and source_is_stream=true.

And in copy_on_write (linux.rs), when source_is_stream is true, it calls copy_stream. So the FIFO should be going through copy_stream!

Maybe the issue is that when opening the file for writing, if it doesn't exist yet, it gets created (by .create(true)), but once it exists, it's only opened for writing without truncation. But in my tests, the destination already exists, and it's still working correctly...

Actually, let me think about this differently. The user says the bug exists. The code clearly has a bug (OpenOptions without truncate). But my tests don't reproduce it. Maybe there's a different code path being taken in my tests than in the actual user scenario.

Looking at the PR description again, they use:
```
wl-paste --watch cp /dev/stdin tmp
```

So `/dev/stdin` is the source. And `/dev/stdin` when you pipe to it is a character device. So it should take the stream path. But in my tests, I'm using `echo "..." | cp /dev/stdin tmp` which might be different from `wl-paste --watch`.

Let me just trust that the bug exists (the code is clearly buggy), and make the fix. The fix is simple: add `.truncate(true)` to the OpenOptions in copy_stream.

    15	use uucore::mode::get_umask;

    17	use crate::{
    18	    CopyDebug, CopyResult, CpError, OffloadReflinkDebug, ReflinkMode, SparseDebug, SparseMode,
    19	};
    20	
    21	/// Copies `source` to `dest` using copy-on-write if possible.
    22	///
    23	/// The `source_is_fifo` flag must be set to `true` if and only if
    24	/// `source` is a FIFO (also known as a named pipe).
    25	pub(crate) fn copy_on_write(
    26	    source: &Path,
    27	    dest: &Path,
    28	    reflink_mode: ReflinkMode,
    29	    sparse_mode: SparseMode,
    30	    context: &str,
    31	    source_is_fifo: bool,
    32	    source_is_stream: bool,
    33	) -> CopyResult<CopyDebug> {
    34	    if sparse_mode != SparseMode::Auto {
    35	        return Err(get_message("cp-error-sparse-not-supported")
    36	            .to_string()
    37	            .into());
    38	    }
    39	    let mut copy_debug = CopyDebug {
    40	        offload: OffloadReflinkDebug::Unknown,
    41	        reflink: OffloadReflinkDebug::Unsupported,
    42	        sparse_detection: SparseDebug::Unsupported,
    43	    };
    44	
    45	    // Extract paths in a form suitable to be passed to a syscall.
    46	    // The unwrap() is safe because they come from the command-line and so contain non nul
    47	    // character.
    48	    let src = CString::new(source.as_os_str().as_bytes()).unwrap();
    49	    let dst = CString::new(dest.as_os_str().as_bytes()).unwrap();
    50	
    51	    // clonefile(2) was introduced in macOS 10.12 so we cannot statically link against it
    52	    // for backward compatibility.
    53	    let clonefile = CString::new("clonefile").unwrap();
    54	    let raw_pfn = unsafe { libc::dlsym(libc::RTLD_NEXT, clonefile.as_ptr()) };
    55	
    56	    let mut error = 0;
    57	    if !raw_pfn.is_null() {
    58	        // Call clonefile(2).
    59	        // Safety: Casting a C function pointer to a rust function value is one of the few
    60	        // blessed uses of `transmute()`.
    61	        unsafe {
    62	            let pfn: extern "C" fn(
    63	                src: *const libc::c_char,
    64	                dst: *const libc::c_char,
    65	                flags: u32,
    66	            ) -> libc::c_int = std::mem::transmute(raw_pfn);
    67	            error = pfn(src.as_ptr(), dst.as_ptr(), 0);
    68	            if std::io::Error::last_os_error().kind() == std::io::ErrorKind::AlreadyExists
    69	                // Only remove the `dest` if the `source` and `dest` are not the same
    70	                && source != dest
    71	            {
    72	                // clonefile(2) fails if the destination exists.  Remove it and try again.  Do not
    73	                // bother to check if removal worked because we're going to try to clone again.
    74	                // first lets make sure the dest file is not read only
    75	                if fs::metadata(dest).is_ok_and(|md| !md.permissions().readonly()) {
    76	                    // remove and copy again
    77	                    // TODO: rewrite this to better match linux behavior
    78	                    // linux first opens the source file and destination file then uses the file
    79	                    // descriptors to do the clone.
    80	                    let _ = fs::remove_file(dest);
    81	                    error = pfn(src.as_ptr(), dst.as_ptr(), 0);
    82	                }
    83	            }
    84	        }
    85	    }
    86	
    87	    if raw_pfn.is_null() || error != 0 {
    88	        // clonefile(2) is either not supported or it errored out (possibly because the FS does not
    89	        // support COW).
    90	        match reflink_mode {
    91	            ReflinkMode::Always => {
    92	                return Err(get_message_with_args(
    93	                    "cp-error-failed-to-clone",
    94	                    HashMap::from([
    95	                        ("source".to_string(), source.display().to_string()),
    96	                        ("dest".to_string(), dest.display().to_string()),
    97	                        ("error".to_string(), error.to_string()),
    98	                    ]),
    99	                )
   100	                .into());
   101	            }
   102	            _ => {
   103	                copy_debug.reflink = OffloadReflinkDebug::Yes;
   104	                if source_is_stream {
   105	                    let mut src_file = File::open(source)?;
   106	                    let mode = 0o622 & !get_umask();
   107	                    let mut dst_file = OpenOptions::new()
   108	                        .create(true)
   109	                        .write(true)
   110	                        .mode(mode)
   111	                        .open(dest)?;
   112	
   113	                    let context = buf_copy::copy_stream(&mut src_file, &mut dst_file)
   114	                        .map_err(|_| std::io::Error::from(std::io::ErrorKind::Other))
   115	                        .map_err(|e| CpError::IoErrContext(e, context.to_owned()))?;
   116	
   117	                    if source_is_fifo {
   118	                        dst_file.set_permissions(src_file.metadata()?.permissions())?;
   119	                    }
   120	                    context
   121	                } else {
   122	                    fs::copy(source, dest)
   123	                        .map_err(|e| CpError::IoErrContext(e, context.to_owned()))?
   124	                }
   125	            }
   126	        };
   127	    }
   128	
   129	    Ok(copy_debug)
   130	}

     6	use std::fs::{self, File, OpenOptions};
     7	use std::os::unix::fs::OpenOptionsExt;
     8	use std::path::Path;
     9	
    10	use uucore::buf_copy;
    11	use uucore::locale::get_message;
    12	use uucore::mode::get_umask;
    13	
    14	use crate::{
    15	    CopyDebug, CopyResult, CpError, OffloadReflinkDebug, ReflinkMode, SparseDebug, SparseMode,
    16	};
    17	
    18	/// Copies `source` to `dest` for systems without copy-on-write
    19	pub(crate) fn copy_on_write(
    20	    source: &Path,
    21	    dest: &Path,
    22	    reflink_mode: ReflinkMode,
    23	    sparse_mode: SparseMode,
    24	    context: &str,
    25	    source_is_fifo: bool,
    26	    source_is_stream: bool,
    27	) -> CopyResult<CopyDebug> {
    28	    if reflink_mode != ReflinkMode::Never {
    29	        return Err(get_message("cp-error-reflink-not-supported")
    30	            .to_string()
    31	            .into());
    32	    }
    33	    if sparse_mode != SparseMode::Auto {
    34	        return Err(get_message("cp-error-sparse-not-supported")
    35	            .to_string()
    36	            .into());
    37	    }
    38	    let copy_debug = CopyDebug {
    39	        offload: OffloadReflinkDebug::Unsupported,
    40	        reflink: OffloadReflinkDebug::Unsupported,
    41	        sparse_detection: SparseDebug::Unsupported,
    42	    };
    43	
    44	    if source_is_stream {
    45	        let mut src_file = File::open(source)?;
    46	        let mode = 0o622 & !get_umask();
    47	        let mut dst_file = OpenOptions::new()
    48	            .create(true)
    49	            .write(true)
    50	            .mode(mode)
    51	            .open(dest)?;
    52	
    53	        buf_copy::copy_stream(&mut src_file, &mut dst_file)
    54	            .map_err(|_| std::io::Error::from(std::io::ErrorKind::Other))
    55	            .map_err(|e| CpError::IoErrContext(e, context.to_owned()))?;
    56	
    57	        if source_is_fifo {
    58	            dst_file.set_permissions(src_file.metadata()?.permissions())?;
    59	        }
    60	        return Ok(copy_debug);
    61	    }
    62	
    63	    fs::copy(source, dest).map_err(|e| CpError::IoErrContext(e, context.to_owned()))?;
    64	
    65	    Ok(copy_debug)
    66	}
